Yangzhong 89

Investigate and Deal with Construction Bureau Staff for Embezzling Public Funds: Since the Yangzhong County Construction Bureau was abolished last spring, it was replaced by the Yangzhong County Construction Office, which is concurrently managed by the Zhenjiang County Construction Bureau. The Zhenjiang Bureau sent technician Cui Hualiang to the office to preside over the work. Since Cui arrived in Yangzhong, he has not achieved any results, and the people of Yangzhong have been very critical. Recently, it was suddenly discovered that he had embezzled public funds. The Construction Department sent personnel to verify the situation. The riverbed of the Yangzhong Er Dunzi Port is higher than the embankment. Because the project is large and expensive, it has not been dredged for a long time. Two years ago, Jiang Wanqing donated 3,000 yuan for the port opening. Later, it was found that the money was insufficient. The former County Party Department and local people agreed that Yuan Tong and Yong Tong He, two businesses, would be responsible for safekeeping, and the money could not be withdrawn until construction started. The two businesses made a record and handed it over to the Construction Office to pay interest at a rate of 1.5% per month. When Cui Hualiang, the technician of the office, collected the interest each month, he only wrote "Interest received for the month of [Month]" on the record, without noting the amount. However, when he reported to the Zhenjiang County Construction Bureau, he only reported that the interest was 8%. Director Zhang of the bureau did not investigate because of some connections. Recently, Guo and Wang, two businessmen from Yangzhong Company, reported the matter to the Construction Department. The Construction Department sent Commissioner Yu Zhongju to Yangzhong to check the ledgers of the two merchants and found that the daily interest rate was indeed 1.5%. Over ten months, technician Cui Hualiang had embezzled more than 200 yuan. He was interrogated at the Construction Office. Cui knew that the matter could not be concealed and agreed to return 210 yuan and wrote a receipt. The department commissioner took it to the province. Cui was afraid that the matter was not over, so he tracked to the province and asked Director Zhang of Zhenjiang to find a way to make amends. It is now heard that all the people's organizations in Yangzhong City will report to the provincial department to severely punish Cui for embezzling public funds, as the evidence is conclusive.

Lumber Company Bankrupt Due to Losses: The Fuyuanyuanlai Lumber Company in Dao Shang Miao Town, Yangzhong, was jointly established by E Wannian, Dai Zhonghua, Chen Feng, and others, and has been in operation for more than ten years. Recently, due to incompetent management, it has suffered losses over the years and owes large amounts of money to lumber companies in Shangxinhe, Nanjing, and Changzhou. Recently, Lou Huiwu, manager of Yihesheng in Shangxinhe, Zheng Yujie, manager of Yonghexiang, Lei Zhuqin, manager of Yongxingyu, Huang Jiexu, manager of Huangtiantai, and Liu Rong, manager of Changzhou Yuanfenghang, came to Yangzhong as representatives of the creditors to negotiate. The shareholders of the company are willing to sell the existing lumber, wooden boards, coffins, and real estate in the warehouse, which are estimated to be worth more than 4,000 yuan, to repay the debt. The remaining debt will be borne by the shareholders. Therefore, the company has now declared bankruptcy.

Yangzhou 90

Two Rickshaw Pullers Drown After Falling into Water with Bridge: Yesterday (5th) afternoon at 2 PM, a woman surnamed Liu, who lives in Six Lane in the city, had accompanied her son back to her home province of Ningbo last month for a visit to relatives at a person surnamed Mao's. Yesterday, because they were returning to sweep tombs for Qingming Festival, they returned by rickshaw. Unexpectedly, when the rickshaw reached the wooden slope of the first bridge (i.e., Dong Bridge), it was difficult to climb the slope because it was heavily loaded. Another empty rickshaw followed behind, so the rickshaw puller put down his own rickshaw and helped the front rickshaw over the slope, but he used too much force, and the railings on both sides of the bridge had been falling off for a long time. As a result, the female passenger, a child, and two rickshaw pullers, as well as the rickshaw itself, all fell into the water. At that time, there was a bean boat parked under the river. The child fell near the boat and was rescued by the boatman. The female passenger, when she fell into the water, held tightly to the large package of cotton clothes she was carrying, so she did not sink immediately and was also rescued by the bean boat. However, both rickshaw pullers drowned, and their bodies have not yet been recovered.

Murder of Husband, Execution by Hanging: Liu, the wife of Lv Jieyou, a farmer in Xixin Village, Anji County, is 40 years old and from Huaining, Anhui Province. She had an affair with Xiong Shiming, a hired hand employed by her husband. After being discovered by her husband, the two conspired to strangle him to death at night. At 9 AM yesterday morning, the male and female convicts were taken out, their identities were verified, and they were immediately tied up and taken to the execution ground, where they were executed by hanging.

Major Fire in Erjingmiao Alley: At about 1 AM yesterday morning, in Wang's house in Erjingmiao Alley in Ningbo City, an old woman, Chen Wang, was careless when cooking, causing a fire. It took two hours to extinguish the fire. Nineteen buildings with multiple stories and forty-four single-story houses were destroyed. Hefei 94

Battle Between Army Units Due to Misunderstanding: A battalion of the newly formed 5th Brigade, Pan Shanzhai's troops, was moving from Luan to Zhengyang. The night before last, when they reached Shaojiawan, a place in the Western Second District of Hefei, they encountered the Western Second Regiment, which was deploying to defend against bandits. Because it was dark, the two sides misunderstood each other and opened fire. The sound of guns and cannons continued all night. It was not until dawn that they realized it was a misunderstanding and stopped fighting. Fei Zhiyuan, a platoon leader of the regiment, was killed in action. Company Commander Wang and six soldiers were captured. Several soldiers were also shot and wounded. Pan Brigade also suffered casualties, including a company commander and more than ten soldiers. The head of the regiment, Liu Wenshu, has now come to the city to report. The county government urgently telegraphed to Pan Brigade to apologize and inquire about the truth.

Local News

Shanghai County Held Relocation Meeting Yesterday 95

90 Yuan per Mu Approved for Land Requisition

3 Yuan for Brick Graves, 2 Yuan for Earth Graves

The Shanghai County Relocation Design Committee held its fifth meeting yesterday. The attendees included Construction Bureau Director Wu Wenhua, County Government Secretary Ye Dezhen, Education Bureau Director Shi She, Party Department Standing Committee Member Lv Zhe, Finance Bureau Director Wang Li (represented by Lu Dingxin), local gentry Niu Changyao (represented by Sun Shengjun), Peng Liren, Property Management Office Shen Zhou, Second District Chief Peng Zhaotang, Third District Chief Yang Fulin, and Sixth District Chief Wang Chengyao (represented by Yang Shunfan), a total of eleven people. The meeting was held at 2 PM in the auditorium on the second floor of the County Government. Director Wu Wenhua presided and Wan Shaoren recorded. The meeting adjourned at 4 PM. The resolutions are recorded below:

Reporting Items: After the meeting began, the chairman first reported: (1) The new county government area has been surveyed by personnel sent by the Construction Bureau. (2) The committee previously wanted to understand the organizational structure of various agencies and the area of the buildings to be used after the relocation, so it sent letters to collect information. Now, various agencies have sent information to the committee one after another. (3) The land requisition method for the new county government area has been submitted by the Construction Bureau and passed by the county political meeting. (4) The land price for the new county government area is 90 yuan per mu. The committee had previously resolved to submit it to the county for approval. An instruction has now been received approving the proposed price.

Discussion Items: Resolutions: (1) Whether the new county government budget sent by Committee Member Wu Wenhua is appropriate is up for discussion. Resolution: Amended and passed. (2) How should the land to be requisitioned first in the new county government area be handled? Resolution: Requisition 50 mu first according to another map. (3) Should a deadline be set for the relocation of graves and other obstacles in the new county government area? Resolution: (a) After surveying the graves and other obstacles within the scope of the area on the 11th of this month, submit a report to the county government to issue a notice requiring all items to be relocated within 30 days. (b) Relocation fees: 3 yuan per grave for brick graves and 2 yuan per grave for earth graves. (4) Should incentive measures be formulated for the establishment of public utilities in the new county government area? Resolution: Committee Members Ye Dezhen, Shi She, and Wu Wenhua are designated to formulate incentive measures for discussion at the next meeting. (5) How should the land requisition procedures be specified in detail? Resolution: (a) The Third District will first conduct a survey and create a register, which will be sent to the Finance and Construction Bureaus for review. (b) The land price will be paid in one lump sum by the Finance and Construction Bureaus on the 15th of this month, sending personnel to the district. (c) Those receiving the payment shall invite the township head and bring the receipt to the district to fill out and collect the payment on time. (d) Those who cannot come to the district to fill out and collect the payment on time must invite the district township head to complete the procedures and collect the payment from the Finance Bureau.

Taxpayer Association

Representative General Assembly Tomorrow 96

Electing Chinese Directors and Committee Members of the Public Works Department and Executive Committee Members

Discussing Promoting Primary School Education and Opposing Rent Assessment and Taxation

The first meeting of the tenth session of the Shanghai Concession Chinese Taxpayers Association is scheduled to be held at 2 PM on the 10th of this month at the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce on North Suzhou Road. Foreign Ships

No Longer Anchoring in the Center of the Huangpu River 97

Customs to Take Over Buoys

The Shanghai Times reports that the National Government has reached an agreement with the diplomatic representatives of the United Kingdom, the United States, France, and Japan that foreign warships will no longer anchor in the center of the Huangpu River. All naval buoys will be handed over to the management of the Customs immediately, and they will no longer have the right to set up fixed anchorages within China's territorial waters. Although Italy does not have naval buoys in the Huangpu River, it is said to have participated in this discussion. In the future, foreign warships coming to Shanghai will anchor between Zhoujiazui and the Huangpu River, or between the buoys of foreign companies, but they must be under the control of the Customs. Therefore, these buoys will also be taken back by the Customs. According to people in the National Government, except for China, no other country currently allows a foreign navy to set up buoys and enjoy fixed anchoring rights in its territorial waters. Moreover, the anchoring of large warships in the center of the Huangpu River obstructs navigation. Therefore, there is a move to take back the naval buoys of various countries. As for naval berths, being farther from the city center should not cause any inconvenience.

The Shanghai Times reports that according to personnel of the Shanghai Electric Tramways, the tram fares in the Public Concession will increase starting this month on the 19th, in order to make up for the increased expenses due to the decline in silver prices. The Issue of Implementing the Factory Law 103

The Industrial and Commercial Management Association Scheduled to Meet on the 11th

to Discuss

Regarding the issue of postponing the implementation of the Factory Law and revising it, there are a total of seven proposals from various parties. After several discussions by the Industrial and Commercial Management Association, it was deemed that the proposal of the Industrial and Commercial Management Association was the most accurate. However, after being distributed to various manufacturers for study, most opinions still intend to revise it. It is learned that this Saturday, the Industrial and Commercial Management Association plans to gather again for discussion to make a final decision. The reporter also interviewed Mr. Qian Chengxu of the China General Federation of Industry on the issue of implementing the Factory Law in foreign factories in the concession and its relationship with the International Labour Office, and asked about the historical process. He replied that in 1919, when China signed the Treaty of Versailles with Germany and Austria, it became a member of the International Labour Organization. The International Labour Conference held in Washington in 1919, especially the National Committee, discussed labor issues in various Far Eastern countries. Regarding the Chinese part, it was hoped that: (1) The Chinese government would adopt the principle of protecting workers with the Factory Law; (2) It was advocated that the International Labour Conference should negotiate with relevant countries to make them follow the labor laws already established by the Chinese government in their concessions and leased territories in China, and that the Chinese government should implement them in the concessions and leased territories. In March 1923, the Chinese government, based on the proposals of the conference, promulgated the Provisional Factory Regulations, and Article 3 clearly stipulated that all foreign factories within the territory of China should be subject to them. The concession authorities were panicked and repeatedly gathered to discuss the matter, and their opinions on this section were: (1) The concession only adopted a part of the principles of the Factory Regulations and separately formulated the Concession Factory Regulations; (2) Consideration was temporarily postponed until extraterritoriality was abolished; (3) If the Chinese government agreed to accept the opinions of the Child Labour Committee, revised the regulations, and could implement them in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces or only in Jiangsu province, the Concession Municipal Council would find ways to obtain the necessary powers to implement them in the concession. Later, due to the divergence of opinions from various parties, it was suspended indefinitely. In 1918, Albert Thomas, the Director-General of the International Labour Office, came to China for sightseeing, and the Chinese government reiterated the previous proposal. At that time, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce had drafted the Factory Law, but Thomas replied that he had not been authorized to do so. In 1929, the International Labour Conference held its twelfth session, and the Chinese government representatives again proposed the "Bill that foreign factories in China should obey the labor laws implemented by the Chinese government." It was rejected due to insufficient votes. The discussant again asked whether the delegation would propose this case at this year's Labour Conference since the delegation had changed its representatives. He replied that the authority was in the government, and the employer representatives could not act alone.

The Ministry of Industry yesterday instructed the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, saying, "Regarding the instruction, recently, according to the report of the Indian Consulate General on the commercial situation in India, the last paragraph briefly states that the commerce of Japan in India has been very developed recently, and its speed of progress is surprising. However, the trade between our country and India has not seen any improvement. As for the goods that Chinese merchants have always handled here, they are only the products needed for daily supply. Recently, due to the Indian boycott of British goods, several overseas Chinese stores have initiated a trial of Chinese-made cigarettes in India. Although these goods are just starting out, the cigarettes that have been transported are quite welcome to the scholars. However, the Shanghai cigarette factory does not deliver the goods in a timely manner, causing the general manager here to have difficulty coping with the shortage of goods. If measures are not taken to supervise them early, there will be a risk of failure. Therefore, it is hereby ordered that the association inform the cigarette factory merchants in the city and urge them to pay close attention to timely delivery to avoid the failure of trade with India." The Municipal Chamber of Commerce has forwarded a letter to the Cigarette Factory Association, urging the cigarette factories to pay attention to timely delivery to avoid the failure of trade with India.

Last Year

Business Conditions of Railways Throughout the Country 105

Total Revenue Reached 104,889,352 Yuan

Excluding the Pinghan, Longhai, Jichang, Zhangxia, Taoang, Shenhai, Jihai, and Jidun railways, which were affected by military operations and for which statistics are not yet available, the operating conditions of the state-owned railways directly under the Ministry of Railways last year (1920) showed varying degrees of increase or decrease, such as the Jinpu Railway. The total revenue of each railway and the comparison with the revenue conditions in 1919 are as follows: The total revenue of the Jinpu Railway in 1920 was 10,786,648 yuan, and the revenue of the railway in 1919 was 11,999,888 yuan, a decrease of 1,213,240 yuan. The total revenue of the Beining Railway in 1920 was 37,439,842 yuan, and the revenue of the railway in 1919 was 37,829,000 yuan, a decrease of 389,158 yuan. The total revenue of the Jinghu Railway in 1920 was 12,558,638 yuan, and the revenue of the railway in 1919 was 12,120,563 yuan, an increase of 477,8075 yuan. The total revenue of the Huhangyong Railway in 1920 was 6,641,712 yuan, and the revenue of the railway in 1919 was 5,855,415 yuan, an increase of 756,297 yuan. The total revenue of the Pingsui Railway in 1920 was 4,667,738 yuan, and the revenue of the railway in 1919 was 5,611,998 yuan, a decrease of 944,260 yuan. The total revenue of the Zhengtai Railway in 1920 was 5,844,200 yuan, and the revenue of the railway in 1919 was 5,172,337 yuan, an increase of 671,863 yuan. The total revenue of the Daoqing Railway in 1920 was 1,406,273 yuan, and the revenue of the railway in 1919 was 993,291 yuan, an increase of 412,982 yuan. The total revenue of the Guangjiu Railway in 1920 was 1,568,044 yuan, and the revenue of the railway in 1919 was 1,396,886 yuan, an increase of 171,158 yuan. The total revenue of the Xiang'e Railway in 1920 was 1,472,330 yuan, and the revenue of the railway in 1919 was 2,188,806 yuan, a decrease of 717,476 yuan. The total revenue of the Jiaoji Railway in 1920 was 12,314,937 yuan, and the revenue of the railway in 1919 was 12,202,249 yuan, an increase of 112,688 yuan. The total revenue of the Nanxun Railway in 1920 was 1,234,379 yuan, and the revenue of the railway in 1919 was 1,439,245 yuan, a decrease of 204,866 yuan. The total revenue of the Guangshao Railway in 1920 was 5,670,454 yuan, and the revenue of the railway in 1919 was 3,625,748 yuan, an increase of 2,044,706 yuan. The total revenue of the Huhai Railway in 1920 was 3,244,157 yuan, and the revenue of the railway in 1919 was 3,353,320 yuan, a decrease of 109,163 yuan. The revenue of the Sidao Railway in 1920 was 7,387,246 yuan. According to the total revenue statistics of the above railways, the total is 104,889,352 yuan, compared with the total revenue of 103,819,746 yuan in 1919, an increase of 1,069,606 yuan.

Shipping News 106

Shipwrecked Crew Rescued: The Japanese ship Chunqing Maru, 4,900 tons, managed by Yamashita in Shanghai, was coming to Shanghai loaded with wheat from Australia on February 5th. That afternoon at 10:00 PM, the ship encountered fog and ran aground at 113 degrees 40 minutes east longitude and 22 degrees 30 minutes north latitude. After the accident, the Meiho Maru and Changfu Maru went to rescue one after another, but they also ran aground. Afterwards, the Meiho Maru rescued the crew, but the bottom of the Chunqing Maru was flooded and could not be towed. The company then sent the Chunbao Maru to rescue the crew. As of yesterday, the Chunbao Maru had rescued all 42 people, including the captain of the Chunqing Maru, Mr. Iida, and the staff, and they have disembarked at the China Merchants Bureau.

Kuaipi Sent to Rescue: The Shanghai Merchants Bureau's Shangjiang vessel, Kuaipi, ran aground near Shashi. The Hankou Bureau sent the Liji vessel to tow it, and the 48th Division sent a team of soldiers to protect the ship.

Japanese Ship Starts Service to Yantai: There are no Japanese ships operating between Shanghai and Yantai. In order to compete with British ships, Dalian Kisen Kaisha has decided to open a new Shanghai-Yantai route. It has been decided that the first voyage on the Shanghai-Yantai line will be on the 17th of this month, using the Changping and Tianjin ships from the Shanghai-Tianjin line. Recently, the company has begun to solicit goods to Yantai and passengers. British ships are also preparing to compete fiercely with it.

The document stated: "After reading today's Shen Bao newspaper, an article on the 'Japanese Ship Fengpumaru Colliding with the Jiangyu Ship,' although fortunately the ship retreated quickly and did not cause the drowning of people, it is clear that in recent years, Japanese ships have been vigorously advancing into our country's inland rivers under the pretext of reciprocal navigation, as if entering an uninhabited area. They run into Chinese ships indiscriminately, causing the tragedies of property and lives of the Xinda Ming and Xinkang ships. At that time, they turned their heads and ignored them, and afterwards, they delayed compensation. This is nothing but the capitalist imperialists of Japan attempting to expand their shipping and deliberately destroying Chinese ships. The intentions of Sima Zhao are obvious. If this can be tolerated, what cannot be tolerated? In order to avoid the baseless disaster of Chinese ship seamen and to maintain our country's shipping rights and sovereignty, the association should send a telegram to the central government, making a serious protest to Japan, and issue a notice to strictly restrict the import of Japanese ships. If there is any violation, they should be stopped with force. As for the damage to the Jiangyu ship this time and the tragedies of the previous Xinda Ming ships, the Japanese side should be ordered to compensate them in the shortest period of time to quell the atmosphere of violence and warn against future offenders. It is reasonable to report this and enclose a copy of the newspaper for your review and implementation." Page 10

Municipal Bonds Regulations

Lottery Drawing Ten Days Before Redemption 113

Revised Municipal Bond Overdue Regulations

The Shanghai Municipal Government previously approved the official letter from the Shanghai Municipal Bond Fund Custody Committee, stating that the lottery drawing dates of the various public bonds issued by the National Government are specified in each set of regulations. However, the revised municipal bond regulations only stipulate the redemption date in Article 8, and the lottery drawing date is not specified. If it is determined on a temporary basis each time, it seems insufficient to show uniformity. It is proposed to predetermine a lottery drawing date within one month before March 31st and September 30th each year. It also seeks guidance on whether the predetermined lottery drawing date should be added to the regulations. The Municipal Government has replied to the committee, stating that the municipal bond regulations have been approved for revision by the government, and it is not necessary to add the lottery drawing date to the regulations again. In the future, the lottery drawing should be held ten days before the redemption date, according to precedent. The original plan for the redemption of Shanghai municipal bonds was 200,000 yuan for each of the first twelve periods, and 300,000 yuan for each of the last two periods. The Municipal Government submitted a request to the Executive Yuan, which was then forwarded to the Legislative Yuan for revision, because the amount did not match the number of lottery tickets. The government has announced the revised regulations. The revised redemption plan is seven lottery tickets for each of the first twelve periods, with each lottery ticket redeeming 33,000 yuan, for a total of 210,000 yuan each. For the last two periods, eight lottery tickets will be drawn each period, and each lottery ticket will redeem 30,000 yuan, for a total of 240,000 yuan each. As for the interest, it was originally 1,188,000 yuan, but according to the revised regulations, only 1,154,400 yuan of interest is required, reducing the interest by 33,600 yuan, which benefits the ticket holders and reduces the burden on the citizens.

Improvement

Fifth Day of the Fisheries Promotion Association 115

Closing Ceremony Scheduled for the Tenth

Yesterday was the fifth day of the Jiangsu Province Shanghai Fisheries Promotion Association. The number of visitors remained crowded, with even more groups visiting than before. More than ten schools, including Wuben, Aiqun, and Qianghua, led their entire student bodies to visit. Zhang Yunlv of Wuben Girls' School sent a letter requesting the association to send a aquaculture expert to lecture at the school. The association has replied, agreeing to the request. In view of the enthusiastic participation of various groups, the association is providing even more preferential treatment to groups, requiring only a letter for admission. The association has now scheduled the closing ceremony for 1:00 PM on the tenth of this month and has sent telegrams to the central, provincial, and municipal governments, provincial and municipal party headquarters, the Department of Agriculture and Mining, and the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, inviting them to send representatives to attend. The location is the Fu'an Cinema in Xiaodongmen. Yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM, a discussion on fisheries improvement was held with aquaculture experts. Attendees included Li Dong, Huang Wenfeng, Yang Zhengqing, Chen Zhengping, Yang Shuheng, Hou Chaohai, Wang Wentai, Li Zhaohui, Wang Defa, Zhang Yousheng, Jin Xinheng, Gu Zhongfu, Wu Huanru, Zhou Jianyin, Wang Liansheng, Chen Moulang, and more than thirty others. Li Dong was elected as chairman, and Chen Moulang as recorder. The meeting proceeded as follows: Report items: (1) Hou Chaohai, chief of the Fisheries Promotion Association, reported the reason for convening the fisheries improvement discussion; (2) Chairman Li Dong reported on behalf of the Ministry of Industry on the central government's fisheries administration plan: (A) Measures have been drafted to ban foreign fishing vessels; (B) To protect fisheries, it is proposed to divide the coastal areas into four zones: Liaoning, Hebei-Shandong, Jiangsu-Zhejiang, and Fujian-Guangdong. Each zone will have a fisheries administration bureau. The objectives are (1) protecting the ocean and (2) enforcing regulations. Each bureau will have an operating budget of 500,000, and five patrol ships. The Jiangsu-Zhejiang Fisheries Administration Bureau will be established first, reorganized from the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Fisheries Affairs Bureau; (C) Maintaining existing fisheries and promoting new-style fisheries. The method of maintaining existing fisheries is to ban inshore trawling to maintain it. Promoting new-style fisheries is divided into five types. It is proposed to start with experiments for promoting new-style fisheries: (1) Establishing a central model aquaculture experiment station with an operating budget of 500,000, divided into three departments: fishing, manufacturing, and aquaculture. When the experiments are successful, two more departments will be added: publicity and training. The central experiment station will be located in Wusong for the manufacturing department, which will be attached to the general station. The fishing department will be located in Shengshan, and the aquaculture department will be divided into two locations: the freshwater department will be located on the Beijing-Shanghai line, and the saltwater department will be located in Sanmen Bay; (2) The central government stipulates that offshore fisheries subsidies will be jointly funded with coastal provinces. The central treasury will spend 250,000, and the coastal provinces will spend 250,000 (36,000 per province); (3) Demarcating subsidy areas and prohibited areas. The subsidy method is 30 yuan per ton of each ship, 25 yuan per horsepower, and 30% for a radio. Each fishing vessel can receive about 20,000 yuan in subsidies for fishing in the subsidy area; (4) In addition to subsidies, there are also grants. All domestic fishing vessels that can fish in the offshore areas will be given half of the subsidy. Foreign fishing vessels that are deemed suitable can also receive a 50% grant; (5) The central government stipulates that the aquaculture administrative fee for the 20th year of the Republic will be 1.5 million yuan, 1 million yuan will be used for the operating expenses of the management bureau, and 500,000 yuan will be used for the operating expenses of the aquaculture farm, which will be allocated from the 80 million industrial public bonds; (3) Hou Chaohai, a technician from the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Agriculture and Mining, reported on Jiangsu Province's fisheries administration, starting with formulating a policy, conducting fisheries surveys, and convening fisheries protection meetings. Recently, they are actively preparing to establish fisheries guidance centers in important coastal fisheries locations; (4) Wu Huanru, section chief of the Shanghai Bureau of Social Affairs, and technician Zhou Jianyin reported successively on the bureau's planned projects and future active opinions on fisheries. Next, discussion items: (1) Contacting aquaculture professionals to seek fisheries improvement, to be handled by the Jiangsu Provincial Branch of the Aquaculture Society; (2) Aquaculture economic survey, to be handled by the Bureau of Social Affairs; (3) Requesting the municipal government to add aquaculture professionals, submitting a request to the municipal government for review; (4) Banning foreign fishing vessels, requesting the Bureau of Social Affairs to assist the central government in carrying out various measures to eliminate foreign fishing vessels in the shortest possible time; (5) Requesting the Ministry of Industry to consult with the Ministry of Education to establish aquaculture vocational schools as soon as possible according to the Ministry of Education's plan and to compile aquaculture textbooks to be distributed to primary schools in coastal provinces and cities to add aquaculture knowledge textbooks; (6) Requesting provincial and municipal governments to establish fisheries guidance centers within the 20th year of the Republic. The rest will be discussed at the next meeting. It was also decided that the Jiangsu Provincial Branch of the Aquaculture Society of the Republic of China would be established today (the 9th).

Complete Suspension of Cotton Cloth and Yarn Production and Transportation 116

Customs Broker Workers Continue Strike

Great Panic Among Shipping and Passenger Groups

Due to the Cotton Cloth Trade Association's ban on cotton cloth cartage fees and inspection fees, the customs broker workers in this city have declared a strike. The authorities have sent personnel to investigate in order to review the matter. Yesterday, various passenger groups panicked. The Chongqing steamer therefore changed its sailing schedule. The details are listed below:

Yesterday's Situation: After the customs broker workers went on strike, the wharves became even quieter yesterday. Xu Shenggui, a member of the sixth team of the customs broker union inspection team, discovered at the Xintang wharf on the Bund of Simalu that workers from Tiantaicheng Company were privately loading three pieces of broadcloth to Niuzhuang and immediately detained them, reporting to the team leader. Upon hearing this, the union sent personnel to negotiate seriously because the workers had violated the strike discipline. Liu Cai, the foreman of the company, immediately went to the union to apologize and settle the matter.

Impact on Shipping: The strike of customs broker workers has a great impact on shipping and the business community. The Taikoo Company's Chongqing steamer, originally scheduled to sail to Andong yesterday afternoon, had no cargo to load due to the strike of customs broker workers and changed its sailing to Friday (the 10th) afternoon. The Hangfu Company's Fuyuan steamer, originally scheduled to go directly to Chongqing today, must wait for the customs broker workers to resume work before sailing. The China Merchants Bureau's Guangli steamer, originally scheduled to sail to Fuzhou on Saturday (the 11th), could not load goods for the construction group due to the strike of customs broker workers. If the customs broker workers still have not resumed work by then, the steamer will inevitably have to change its schedule as well.

Panic Among Various Groups: Various passenger groups in Fujian, Yantai, Niuzhuang, Tianjin, Andong, Qingdao, Weihaiwei, Hankou, Yichang, Chongqing, Jiujiang, Changsha, Anqing, Wanxian, Shashi, etc., because the Consolidated Tax Bureau will treat all cotton yarn and cotton cloth with permits issued before April 15 as new goods and collect new taxes according to regulations. Therefore, after the customs broker workers went on strike, those who had ordered goods from foreign firms were worried about the strike being prolonged and panicked. Yesterday, the San Shan Guild Hall in Hubei, Shanghai, sent a letter to the customs broker union, saying, "We have received your union's reply stating that the suspension of work on foreign cloth will inevitably be followed by cotton yarn, which is due to procedures and not intentional. Reading it, we are even more doubtful. Foreign cloth and cotton yarn are clearly two different categories. Your union's suspension of work on foreign cloth is to prompt the foreign cloth group to realize and also reject our group. What effect will this have? Our group has no power to cooperate with your union in negotiating with the foreign cloth group. Aren't we being innocently implicated? Moreover, the new regulations will be implemented on April 16. If the cotton yarn our group is currently purchasing is not loaded before the 16th, we will have to bear another tax burden. At a time when the yarn industry is declining, how can we bear repeated losses? We sincerely hope that your union will understand the situation and immediately notify the workers to allow our group's cotton yarn to be loaded on the next vessel as a special consideration. We look forward to public cooperation."

Guild Hall Meeting: The Cotton Cloth Trade Association held a special emergency executive committee meeting at 2:00 PM yesterday to discuss the strike issue of the customs broker union. All committee members attended, chaired by Chen Shunian. It was resolved: (1) To submit a request to the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs to order the customs broker workers to resume work as soon as possible; (2) To publish a notice in the newspaper immediately to correct the customs broker union's announcement.

Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities

Establishment of a Specialized Problem Research Group 117

Private Public Utilities and Other Areas

If there are Problems, Research can be Commissioned

The Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities is responsible for the administration of public utilities and public enterprises in the city, such as water, electricity, gas, land and water transportation, and wharf warehouses. In recent years, the business has expanded, and the number of technical, health, and administrative issues has increased accordingly. In order to improve administrative efficiency, the bureau has specially formulated methods for grouping and researching specialized problems. According to the scope of the bureau's business, the technical aspect is divided into six groups: water supply engineering, civil engineering, strong electrical engineering, weak electrical engineering, thermal engineering, and transportation engineering. The administrative aspect is divided into seven groups: legal system, personnel, documents, compilation, accounting, general affairs, and business. Personnel within the bureau who specialize in a certain type of engineering or are familiar with a certain type of administrative affair participate in the organization. It is heard that the groups have been established, and when problems arise, they are handed over to the relevant group for collective discussion and appropriate resolution. It is also heard that in addition to problems arising within the bureau, all municipal agencies, private public utility companies in the city, or other parties who encounter problems within the scope of the above-mentioned technical groups can also commission the bureau to issue them for research.

Recent News on the Promotion of the New System of Weights and Measures 118

The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs previously received an order from the Ministry of Industry, approving July 1 of this year as the deadline for announcing the completion of the unification of weights and measures. It has been instructed to inform the Municipal Weights and Measures Calibration Office to instruct all manufacturers and stores in the city to manufacture weights and measures in accordance with the provisions of Article 10, Paragraph 3 of the National Weights and Measures Unification Procedure, ordering them to stop manufacturing old instruments and transform them into new instruments. It has also been ordered to instruct all vegetable markets in the city to advance the use of new instruments from June 1 of this year. Now that the bureau is approaching the date of unification, it is issuing orders to various industry trade associations to inform their members to actively prepare and uniformly comply with the new system from July 1 of this year. As for the types and quantities of various instruments required by each industry, they can be listed in detail and reported directly to the Municipal Weights and Measures Calibration Office on Xieqiao Manufacturing Bureau Road, which will instruct them to rush production so that they can be used as scheduled. Those who delay or wait and see will be severely punished.

On behalf of all the disaster victims in Shaanxi, we respectfully express our gratitude." It is heard that no fewer than eight million people in the province are waiting to be fed. Therefore, the committee is seeking help from all philanthropists to quickly rescue the current crisis.

Young Girl, Unable to Bear Step-Mother's Abuse, Attempts Suicide in River, Fortunately Rescued 126

At about 7:00 PM the day before yesterday, a young girl boarded a Lujiadu ferry at the Ning Shao Wharf on the Sixteenth Bund. Just as the ferry was about to reach the Pudong Wharf and before it had docked, the girl suddenly emerged from the crowd and jumped into the river to commit suicide. At that time, it was just getting dark, and the boatmen could not rescue her. Fortunately, her body floated to the surface for a moment and was rescued by a nearby boatman. She was rescued and immediately sent to the police at the ferry terminal and taken to the third district of the Public Security Bureau. According to the girl's statement, her surname is Yang, her name is Jinzhu, she is 15 years old, from Nanjing, and lives at 1 Rongxiangli, Fangbang Road. Her father's name is Yang Laojiu, and he works as an insurance agent on the Xinshandaolun steamer. Her biological mother passed away five years ago, and her father remarried a stepmother (i.e., her stepmother), Li, four years ago. She is often abused by her stepmother and cannot bear the oppression. Her father is not often at home, so she has no one to tell her sorrows to. She had no choice but to jump into the river to commit suicide. The district chief felt that her situation was very pitiful and ordered the police to summon Li to the district yesterday morning. Li stated that she was 26 years old and had not abused Jinzhu. She requested an investigation. The district chief sent a letter to the relevant Second Section of the First District to investigate and handle the matter.

Hangzhou Taifu Company, which has been operating on Qinghefang Damalu for several years, sells a wide range of domestic fine art porcelain and enameled steel utensils, etc., and has a remarkable reputation. Local News Two

Unfathomable Intentions of Ye Zhongfang 131

Sixteen Letters Filled with Tender Emotion

Soon to Return to Shanghai to Meet Shirley

Trial Postponed to the 23rd for Further Hearing

Must Appear in Court or Face Arrest

Ye Zhongfang, grandson of the late Ye Chengyuan, nicknamed "Little Shaker," informally married Chen Xiuzhen, daughter of Chen Zhigang, who had served as a translator for lawyer Gan Weilu before going to Wuxi and being killed by bandits, the year before last. After his legal wife, née Lu, found out, she frequently scolded him. Ye then began to feel the pain of a husband caught between his wife and concubine, and abandoned his sweet home, moving far away to live a lonely life, neglecting his family affairs. Recently, Ye's wife, née Lu, believing that her husband's departure was solely caused by Xiuzhen, specifically accused her at the French Concession court. Chen Yan, Xiuzhen's mother, because the Ye family lived on Jiaozhou Road, also hired lawyer Xue Jiaqi to accuse Ye Zhongfang in the Special District Local Court of seducing her daughter. The original complaint is as follows:

Original Complaint: This is a private prosecution for the defendant's continuous intent to commit adultery and seduce a woman under the age of twenty away from the person who has parental rights, in violation of Article 257, paragraph 2 of the Criminal Law. The facts of the defendant's crime are stated below: The private prosecutor's biological daughter, Chen Xiuzhen, is currently nineteen years old. She was formerly a dancer at the Chang'e Dance Hall in Shanghai, known as Shirley. In May of the eighteenth year of the Republic of China, the defendant came to the dance hall to dance, and became acquainted with Xiuzhen. Admiring Xiuzhen's beauty, he immediately intended to seduce her. He often took her to play in his room at the Fanwang Palace Hotel and the Cangzhou Restaurant. After a long period of intimacy, the defendant used enticements, dazzling Xiuzhen with his wealth, and claiming that he was on bad terms with his wife and would marry her as his legal wife after divorcing her. Through various deceptions, in June or July of the eighteenth year of the Republic of China, he seduced Xiuzhen to the Far East Hotel to commit adultery in a private room. Afterwards, he continued to commit adultery in hotel rooms. At that time, Xiuzhen was only seventeen years old and weak-willed. After being seduced by him, she concealed the matter from the private prosecutor. Until the morning of December 22nd of the same year, the defendant suddenly came to the private prosecutor's home to visit Xiuzhen, falsely claiming that they would go out for breakfast and return. Unexpectedly, she never returned, disappearing like a yellow crane. Waiting until the 25th, the private prosecutor reported the abduction to the French Concession Lujiiawan Police Station. However, the defendant had lured Xiuzhen away and lodged with her in Room 11 of the Xinxin Society. On the 26th of the same month, he rented a house at No. 45, Mingde Lane, Fuxu Road, second floor. Until January 17th of last year, the defendant and Xiuzhen went together to lawyer Jiang Baoli's office and signed a husband-concubine contract (three copies in total, each holding one copy, with the remaining copy at lawyer Jiang's office). Later, Xiuzhen returned home and told the private prosecutor what had happened. The private prosecutor learned that Xiuzhen had lost her virginity to the defendant long ago. The matter was a fait accompli and could not be undone, so she had to tolerate it. Unexpectedly, on March 1st of this year, the defendant suddenly quarreled with Xiuzhen and sent her back to the private prosecutor's home, abandoning her. He instigated his mother, Ye Peng, and his wife, Lu Yinglan, to fabricate the fact that the defendant had left home due to heartbreak, and hired a lawyer to falsely accuse Xiuzhen of fraud and assault, using newspaper publicity as a method of intimidating the private prosecutor. These are the facts of the defendant's crime. Xiuzhen is currently nineteen years old and not yet an adult. According to the law, she should be under the guardianship of the private prosecutor. The defendant repeatedly seduced her to go out and lodge, clearly violating Article 257, paragraph 2 of the Criminal Law, intending to commit adultery and seduce a woman under the age of twenty away from the person who has parental rights. Although the private prosecutor later became aware of the matter and tolerated it, this is not sufficient to preclude its illegality. Therefore, this complaint is filed, requesting the Honorable Court to promptly issue a warrant to arrest the defendant Ye Zhongfang for trial according to the law, for the sake of justice. Respectfully submitted.

Request for Postponement: According to the complaint, the court originally scheduled a closed hearing for the afternoon of the 6th of this month. However, because that day was a holiday, it was rescheduled to 2:00 PM yesterday in the Third Court, presided over by Judge Xiao Xiecai. The plaintiff, Chen Yan, and her daughter, Xiuzhen, along with their lawyer, Xue Jiaqi, etc., arrived on time. The defendant, Ye Zhongfang, did not appear. Lawyers Yan Jiangyi and Dong Yu defended him. According to the lawyer, the defendant had already left Shanghai before this case occurred. His family received the summons and immediately entrusted lawyer Jiang to publish a notice of the hearing date in the newspaper, but he still has not returned to Shanghai and the hearing should be postponed to allow for further notice.

Continued Hearing Rescheduled: Judge Xiao then summoned Chen Yan for questioning regarding her age and address. According to her statement, she is currently forty years old and resides at No. 19, Guangshun Lane, Mother's Hospital Road, French Concession. Her lawyer then presented a recent letter from the defendant to Chen's daughter. It was clear that the defendant knew he had been accused and was intentionally avoiding appearing in court. The judge should issue an arrest warrant. Judge Xiao stated that the defendant should not be afraid to appear, but out of consideration for the first hearing, he ordered that the hearing be rescheduled to the afternoon of the 23rd of this month. If he still avoids appearing at that time, he will be arrested. Chen Yan and others then left.

Sixteen Letters: It is said that Ye, after hearing that he had been accused, still frequently exchanged letters with Chen Xiuzhen. To date, Xiuzhen has received as many as sixteen handwritten letters from him. Although none of them clearly state the place of origin, examining the postmarks on the envelopes reveals that they were all sent from Nanjing or Pukou. Only one letter was mailed in Beijing. The wording of each letter mostly contains repentance and sorrow, indicating that his heart is full of complaints, which he cannot express and unconsciously reveals between the lines. Several letters also contain attachments, such as the article "A Love Letter is Worth a Love Novel" recently published in the "Kuaihuo Lin" section of the Xinwen Bao, which was enclosed with the letter sent from Beijing. Also enclosed with a letter was a newspaper advertisement with the heading "The Falling Flower is Intentional, but the Flowing Water is Heartless," and on the back of which was written, "The result of me and you, such a pitiful past, unbearable to recall."

Two Photographs: There are two letters with attached photographs. One contains a photograph of the Sword Testing Rock at Tiger Hill, with the following poem by Cui Hu written on the front: "Last year, on this day, in this gate, a face and peach blossoms reflected each other's red. Where has the face gone? The peach blossoms still smile in the east wind." At the back of the photograph is added that it was taken with difficulty while recovering from spitting blood, and sent as a keepsake. This letter was sent from Nanjing. On the "back" of the envelope is written: "Last year we visited together, this year I wander alone. Thinking of the past, I am so sad. Li, the person I love in my life, you and I were in love for so many days, but unfortunately we separated. This photo was taken with difficulty while spitting blood, so it doesn't look like me. I'm sending it to you as a keepsake." The other contains a photo of Ye Zhongfang sitting in a rickshaw, only an inch long and about three-tenths of an inch wide. Several words are written on the back of the envelope: "This photo in the envelope was taken before I took the exam. After this, I may live, I may die, maybe this is my last photo. Cut it out and send it to you, I wonder if you will accept it, my beloved." On the back of the photo is written, "Li, if you still love me, please keep this photo. Zhong."

Recent Letter: On April 4th, another letter was sent from Nanjing, saying: "Li, I ran into an acquaintance from Shanghai in this unfortunate place. Unable to avoid him, I stood on the street and talked for a long time. He said that you recently hired Mr. Yao from Tebak. (Alas, my lifelong friend, why are there so many people who are just doing their jobs? The ways of the world.) Actually, why bother? When I was in Nanjing, I already asked someone to make a long-distance call, asking my family to withdraw the lawsuit. He also said that the Special District Court wants me to appear in court to confront you because of your mother's accusation against me. Originally, I am now a person in uniform, someone who is only subject to military law, but in order to express the bitterness and sorrow in my heart before the judge, I am determined to find a way to take leave and return to Shanghai when necessary. I will meet you with this thin, ghost-like face in a place I don't want to see you. Alas, pitiful Li, you are determined to break up with me. You don't want to remember the past, and in the future, you will follow "someone else." Alas, the person I love so much, you are gone with everything unwilling, leaving me alone, like a fool, looking back and forth. The most tragic thing in the world is nothing more painful than this. Soon, maybe I will see you. When I see you, can you allow me to talk to you a few words? This is my only hope in life. Thinking about where I will see you, my heart becomes sad again. I am ashamed of myself, why don't I have the courage to commit suicide? If I die, everything will be over. I am very sad and can't write anymore. Looking back on the past, it seems like a spring dream. Alas, goodbye. I wish you a bright future and boundless happiness."

Husband-Concubine Contract: The contract is made between Ye Zhongfang, a native of Zhenhai County, Zhejiang Province, currently twenty-two years old (hereinafter referred to as Party A), and Chen Xiuzhen, a native of Shanghai County, Jiangsu Province, currently eighteen years old (hereinafter referred to as Party B). Because both parties are in love and willing to form a husband-concubine relationship, they specially agree to the following: (1) Party A shall provide Party B with food, clothing, and shelter, and shall not abandon Party B forever. If this agreement is violated, Party A shall be liable to pay alimony of 20,000 yuan at one time. (2) Party A agrees not to engage in promiscuous behavior in the future. (3) Party B is willing to fulfill her duties as a wife in every way. If there is any unchaste behavior, in addition to being subject to legal sanctions, Party A shall be entitled to terminate the relationship and no longer demand any alimony. (4) Party B acknowledges that this agreement is made voluntarily. If any problems arise with her family, she shall be responsible for resolving them and shall not cause any difficulty for Party A. January 7th, nineteenth year of the Republic of China. Contract makers: Ye Zhongfang, Chen Xiuzhen. Witnessing Lawyer: Zhuang Baoli.

Harrison Formally Proposes

Purchasing the Dahua Hotel 132

Co-signed by Fei Wusheng of the YMCA

Requesting Discussion at the Annual Meeting of Western Taxpayers

The Shanghai Times reports that the proposal to nationalize the land of the Dahua Hotel in western Shanghai, which was previously deemed wasteful and of little practical benefit by the Board of Directors of the Public Works Department and was not approved, has now been drafted into a resolution by the original proposer, Harrison, and co-signed by Fei Wusheng, General Secretary of the YMCA, and submitted to the Public Works Department for inclusion in the agenda of the Annual Meeting of Western Taxpayers on the 15th of this month. The content roughly states that if the Dahua Hotel land can be purchased at a price deemed reasonable by the Public Works Department, and the city treasury can simultaneously afford to add necessary open space in more densely populated areas within the concession, should the government purchase the hotel land as a park and city hall be considered? Respectfully awaiting public decision.

Suspicious Pedestrian

Shot Dead by Detectives 133

Resisted Inspection

Turned and Fired Back

Detective Li Returned Fire

Resulting in Instant Death

At 3:30 AM yesterday, detectives Kong Qingping and Li Dacheng of the Putuo Road Police Station were patrolling the corner of Binlang Road and Xiaoshadu Road when a man, about thirty years old, suddenly rushed forward from behind. The two detectives, seeing his suspicious behavior, ordered him to stop for inspection. However, the man ignored them and continued to run as before. The two detectives also quickly gave chase. Near a bamboo fence, the man suddenly stopped, turned around, and fired a shot backwards. Detective Kong ducked to the ground to avoid it, and Detective Li immediately drew his gun and returned fire, firing six shots in succession. The bullets hit the man's head, hand, and other parts in three places, and he immediately fell to the ground and died. The detectives then seized the handgun he was holding, which was still loaded with seven bullets. They then carried the body to the forensic examination office on Feilun Road. At 10:00 AM, they reported to the Special District Local Court and commissioned Inspector Guo to come to the office for inspection. He took his seat, and Detectives Kong and Li reported the circumstances of the deceased's resistance to arrest at the time, and stated that because he was killed on the spot and no relatives were found, they did not know the deceased's name, origin, or address. Mr. Guo then instructed the Pushan Villa to claim the body for burial.

Zhejiang Industrial Bank

Savings Department Chief Embezzles Funds 134

Misappropriated 64,000 Yuan

Further Investigation Awaits Recovery

Chen Mutao, a native of Jiaxing and deputy chief of the Savings Department of the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, recently fell ill and requested leave to be treated at the Shanghai Municipal Hospital on Xuejia浜 in the Nanshi district. The president of the bank assigned someone to take over his duties. After investigation, evidence of Chen's continuous embezzlement was discovered, with the amount of savings misappropriated reaching 64,000 yuan. The president of the bank then reported to the General Police Station, dispatching detectives Wu Chunrong and Qian Xianting to the hospital to question Chen. Because Chen had committed embezzlement, if he was not closely monitored, it would be difficult to prevent him from taking the opportunity to escape after recovery. Therefore, Chen was transferred to a hospital established by the Public Works Department for treatment and monitoring. Chen also admitted to embezzling bank funds without denying it, claiming that it was all spent on subsidizing his younger brother's tuition, etc. Yesterday morning, the police station's lawyer, Ru Baoyi, stated to the Special District Local Court that the case could only be investigated after he recovered. Judge Xu approved the request after review.

Aiglun Road

A Man Assassinated 135

Reportedly Caused by Jealousy

Around 12:00 PM the night before last, a man, Mr. Jia, about thirty years old, dressed in plain clothes and resembling someone from northern Jiangsu, was assassinated by his enemies in the Beichujia Bridge area of Aiglun Road in the French Concession. He was shot and wounded in the head and right flank, falling to the ground and dying. Passersby saw the incident and reported it to the police station, ordering detectives to investigate. It was found that the body was lying in a pool of blood, wearing a gray cloth-lined velvet jacket, a blue-gray serge jacket, a new white-bottomed blue-striped short shirt, and a white guidi silk shirt. The lower body was wearing gray cloth trousers with tied leggings, a white material melon-skin cap, and white socks. There were two gold teeth in the mouth. Gunshots entered from the left eyebrow and the right cheek, and fresh blood flowed out. More than a dozen pawn tickets and dozens of cards given by others were found on his body. The detectives reported the situation to the police chief and had the body moved to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Mortuary for forensic examination. No relatives were found. Yesterday, the Criminal Section of the French Police Station reported to Judge Zhu of the French Court for forensic examination. It was confirmed that the deceased had been shot and killed. An order was given to take photos, and the court provided a coffin for collection and temporary storage, awaiting relatives to claim the body. The police station will investigate and bring the murderers to justice. It is said that Mr. Jia was assassinated because of jealousy over a prostitute.

Ewo Fusheng Steamer

Large Quantities of Passenger Cargo Stolen 136

Stolen Ramie Fabric and Rayon

Losses Around 10,000 Yuan

Yesterday, a large batch of cargo was stolen from the Ewo Fusheng, a steamer of the Ewo Yiyang Company, while loading goods in Shanghai. The reporter went to various places to investigate the details of the incident as follows:

Loading and Transporting Cigarettes: The Fusheng is a regular northbound ship of the British-owned Ewo Yiyang Company, scheduled to go to Tianjin yesterday, as well as Yantai via the bay. Yesterday, the ship was docked at the Gonghexiang Wharf in Hongkou to load goods. When the Yantai passenger cargo was being loaded, it was discovered that a large number of valuable cargo items, amounting to more than sixty pieces, had been stolen from the ship. This could not have been done by one or two people. After the ship's staff discovered the theft, they conducted a thorough investigation, but to no avail.

Amount of Cargo Stolen: Among the exports of the Fusheng this time, there were sixty-six pieces of ramie fabric from the Yuelai Public Report of this port being transported to Yantai (S2 Shengli Mark), and one piece of rayon with the VYK brand, all being delivered from Shanghai to Zhifu. Because the goods were valuable, they were ordered to be loaded into the secure cabin to show caution when they were unloaded from the ship. The goods were unloaded on the night of the 7th, and the theft was discovered yesterday morning. It is expected that the theft took place in the latter half of the night of the 7th.

Reporting to the Police for Investigation: The estimated value of the sixty-seven pieces of stolen goods is about 6,000 taels. At that time, the ship's crew searched the ship thoroughly without success and reported to the head office. On the one hand, the Dongyue Public Report Customs Broker was notified that the losses were too great, and that the theft of goods from the secure cabin would hinder future transportation. Therefore, both Yiyang and Dongyue Public Report reported the matter to the water and land police and the concession police station for investigation. The cargo owner also offered a reward for information leading to the arrest of the thieves. A reward of 100 yuan will be given to those who provide information leading to the cracking of the case. If the goods can be recovered, a reward of 10% of the value of the goods will be given.

Fusheng Export: Yesterday, the Fusheng completed the loading of goods and passengers as usual and cleared customs. It left Shanghai at 2:00 PM and went directly to Tianjin via the bay. The theft case will be investigated in Shanghai, with the hope of solving it soon.

Further News on the Demolition of Gelao Archway 139

Xianji Road Renamed Guangqi Road

The Gelao Archway on Xianji Road (縣基路) was built in the early years of the Kangxi reign of the Qing Dynasty. As it straddled the road, it significantly obstructed traffic. Due to its age and lack of repair, it was dilapidated and in danger of collapse. The upper stone material had been largely fractured after a fire. Even if repairs were desired, there was no way to proceed. Previously, the municipal authorities of this city renovated and improved the buildings on the west side of the road, and the old buildings on the east side are also awaiting demolition. The archway posed numerous safety hazards, and leaving it isolated in the middle of the road was risky. If struck by a heavy vehicle, the upper stone material could collapse at any time. For public safety and convenience of traffic, it was better to dismantle it as soon as possible. It is now reported that the Gelao Archway was completely demolished the day before yesterday. All the dismantled stone materials were handed over to Xu Cheng-zong (徐承宗) and others, descendants of the archway's namesake, for preservation. The municipal government, in order to permanently commemorate Xu Guangqi (徐光啓), a Ming Dynasty scholar, for whom the archway was originally built, has renamed Xianji Road as Guangqi Road (光啓路). This is to show that even while reorganizing municipal affairs, the intention to remember past sages is not forgotten.

Hygiene Work of the Chinese Red Cross 140

Vaccinations and Injections: More Men Than Women

Due to the rampant epidemic, the Chinese Red Cross recently organized a hygiene team to administer smallpox vaccinations and preventive injections in both the Chinese and foreign concessions. Starting from the 6th, for a total of three days, preventive injections were administered to 165 men and 30 women in Wangping Street (望平街), Route Massenet (馬立司路), Hardoon Road (哈同路), Caojiadu (曹家渡), and Xiaoshadu Road (小沙渡路). Smallpox vaccinations were given to 42 men and 36 women.

Continued Hearing on the Homicide Case 141

A Japanese Man, Fujii Tatsunosuke, Testifies

The Grandmother of the Deceased Cries Loudly in Court

In addition to the deceased's grandmother, Lu Yang-shi (陸楊氏), and the deceased's wife, Lu Liu-shi (陸劉氏), bringing several children to court to cry and appeal, a Japanese man named Fujii Tatsunosuke (籐井辰之助) was unexpectedly called to testify. Municipal Health Bureau

Suppression of Ankang Yisi Pills 142

The German company Koch & Co. (高吉洋行) on Museum Road (博物院路) in this port sells a kind of Ankang Yisi pills, namely Okasa. Previously, the Central Health Experiment Institute legally tested the pills and found that they contained yohimbine, a poisonous plant alkaloid. The company was warned, and the Municipal Health Bureau sent a letter to the Public Security Bureau to strictly prohibit the sale of the pills. Recently, the company has resumed publishing advertisements in newspapers, arbitrarily promoting the pills and using letters from unqualified and unregistered doctors to promote them. The Municipal Health Bureau considers these pills to be indecent and harmful to the health of citizens. If they are not effectively prohibited, the source of harm cannot be eliminated. It is reported that the bureau has notified the Daily Newspaper Association (日報公會), instructing all newspaper offices to refuse to publish advertisements for these pills in the future. At the same time, it has sent letters to the Public Security Bureau, ordering its subordinate departments to strictly prohibit the sale of the pills, and also sent letters to the police stations of the British and French concessions to prohibit them as well.

Large Rent Increase in Fukang Lane 144

Tenants Petition for Cancellation

The houses in Fukang Lane (福康里) on Xinza Road (新閘路) are owned by the Xi (奚) family, wealthy dye merchants, and were all built more than ten years ago. The residents are all legitimate merchants and have always paid their rent on time. Recently, it was heard that the landlord suddenly issued a notice proposing to uniformly increase the rent by several percent, with some increases as high as 40%. The land in this area was neither newly purchased at a high price, nor is it comparable to building houses on rented land. In this autumn of expensive gold, cheap silver, pearl rice, and cinnamon firewood, all merchants and common people are feeling the pain. Therefore, all the tenants in the lane find it impossible to accept this rent increase. Yesterday, they organized a tenants' association and sent a letter to the landlord, requesting immediate cancellation. They are currently actively pursuing this goal and will not stop until it is achieved. It is hoped that the landlord will take this situation into consideration and find a satisfactory solution.

Verdict in the Counterfeit Anli Cosmetics Case 150

Wu Hong-shou Found Not Guilty

Wu Hong-shou (吳鴻壽) and his wife, Ms. Jin (金), opened the Anli Cosmetics store. Their products, such as Zhilan Cream (芝蘭霜) and Snow Cream, were popular among women and sold widely in various ports. This caused jealousy among foreigners, and the German company Melchers & Co. (美最時洋行) sued Wu in the Special District Court, claiming that Zhilan Cream was similar to their product, "4711" Floral Cream, and was therefore a counterfeit. Wu argued that Zhilan Cream was completely different from "4711" and that the plaintiff's accusation was false. He hired lawyers Zhang Jia-hui (張嘉惠) and Li Jun-huan (李鈞寰) to counter-sue the company's German manager, Huide-men (惠德門), for false accusation. After the Special Court concluded its investigation, the verdict was announced yesterday afternoon by Judge Cheng Shang-feng (程尙豐). Wu Hong-shou was found not guilty, and Huide-men was also found not guilty.

A man named Song (宋) from Songjiang (松江) was recently arrested in Qingdao for selling counterfeit banknotes.

Features of the Youth Film Projector 155

The Pathé Youth Film Projector comes in 100-yard, 20-yard, 10-yard, and 3-yard models. It is small, exquisite, and projects a clear image. The films include detective, romance, war, scenery, and educational subjects. Each screening can entertain two or three hundred people. In rural areas without electricity, you can purchase a Broadcaster dynamo to power the projector. Currently, Baofang Company (寳芳公司) next to Tiannan Hotel (天南旅館) on Avenue Edward VII, as well as the branch stores on Great Horse Road (大馬路) and Fourth Horse Road (四馬路), are offering special low prices to benefit customers, and welcome everyone to visit and view the projectors.

Seventh Issue of "Movie Monthly" Published 156

The "Movie Monthly," edited by Zhou Shi-xun (周世勳) and published by Wenhua Company (文華公司), has been well-received since its publication. Orders from various places have been extremely enthusiastic. To benefit readers, the company has maintained the original price without increasing it despite the soaring cost of paper. The seventh issue of the magazine has been published today. In addition to over twenty interesting articles and a hundred copperplate illustrations, it also features four special articles: "Chaplin's View of Love," "A Day with Greta Garbo," and "The Art of Love," all of which are valuable works. The price of each issue is 30 cents, and the annual subscription is three yuan, with a free "Short History of Movie Stars" included.

North China Defeats Central China 2-1 Yesterday 162

Scoreless in the First Half, Each Team Scores One Goal in the Second Half

North China Scores Again in Extra Time to Win

—East China Plays Central China Tomorrow at 4:00 PM—

The National Zonal Football Championship is in full swing. Yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM, the competition opened at the Chinese Baseball Field (中華棒球塲). North China and Central China played the first match. As a result, North China defeated Central China 2-1 in thirty minutes of extra time. North China has won the first match and entered the final stage. Yesterday, the spring chill was crisp and the wind was quite cold. About three or four thousand spectators were present, sitting precariously in the cold air to appreciate the art of the athletes from North and Central China.

Battle Report 164

North China Attacks Fiercely in One Go

The North China team, wearing uniforms half blue and half white, lined up facing south. The Central China generals, in yellow and red uniforms, symbolized the iron-blooded doctrine they embraced, and prepared to march north. Referee Chen Ji-xiang (陳吉祥) blew a silver whistle, and the battle began. North China kicked off. Zhao 　Feng 　looked into the distance, passing the ball to the right. Huang Yu-jia advanced quickly, and Central China's left back Cheng Guo-yin, in this critical moment, let him slip past, resulting in a corner kick. Huang Yu-jia's shot was excellent, and Huang Zhen-sheng shot fiercely, but the ball went over the bar. In an instant, North China's five forwards arrived together, their coordination excellent and their speed swift. The Central China goal area was dominated by North China's forwards. Judging from this situation, it was clear that North China would prevail.

Central China Seizes the Opportunity to Counterattack 165

Central China tried its best to defend in this critical situation, and immediately counterattacked at the first opportunity. Li Ben-xin passed the ball to Wang Yi-de, a great opportunity, but North China's defense was weak. Unfortunately, the pass was weak and was intercepted. Xiao Bo passed the ball far to the center forward, and Wang Chang-ying also lost his footing. Central China had a great opportunity, but there was not enough support, and the effort failed. Yu Ke-ding passed the ball, and Yuan, the center forward, dribbled left and right. Xian Zhong-fen tried to stop him but failed, and fortunately Wang 　Wei arrived to kick the ball out of bounds. Central China's momentum should not be underestimated. Later, although North China attacked fiercely again, they failed to score, which they regretted. The first half ended with a score of 0-0.

North China Scores with a Thunderclap 166

After the break, Central China kicked off. Huang Zhi-min intercepted the ball, and Huang Yu-jia skipped through three checkpoints, resulting in a corner kick. North China maintained its advantage. Xian Zhong-fen kicked the ball to the Central China goal area, and Zhao, the center forward, kicked the ball, thinking it would surely go in, but it went wide by a few inches. North China had many such opportunities, but they were either inaccurate or weak. The game was chaotic and indecisive, with no clear advantage. Suddenly, with a thunderclap, Huang Zhi-min kicked the ball, hitting the crossbar and bouncing into the net. This boosted their morale. There were still ten minutes left in the game.

Central China Scores in a Swarm 167

North China took the lead with one goal. Judging from Central China's situation, victory seemed nineteen to one in favor of the North. However, North China's center back Zhang Guo-wei injured his foot and left the game, and Huang Yu-jia retreated to replace him. Central China took the opportunity to counterattack. Li Pi-zu and Wang Yi-de advanced together and sent the ball flying into the goal area. Soldiers from all directions arrived, and Huang Zhen-xun, despite his strength, was at a loss. He was surrounded, and Yuan Qing-wu, taking advantage of the situation, sent the ball into the goal. Two minutes later, the game ended. Each team scored one goal, and an extra thirty minutes was announced.

North China Wins in Extra Time 168

During the thirty minutes of extra time, both teams showed signs of fatigue. Central China defended strictly, and North China attacked fiercely. Zhao Qi-zhe passed the ball to the left, and Zhang De-jiang advanced quickly. Huang Zhi-min headed the ball, but it was not accurate and did not go into the net. Although North China was playing with only ten men, they still had the upper hand. Zhang De-jiang took a corner kick, and the ball hovered in front of the goal. Huang Zhi-min landed his foot on the ground and shot, but the ball rolled into the goalkeeper's hands. Tang Shun-hua kicked, but although he did not kick it in, it had already crossed the white line. The referee then announced that North China had won 2-1.

Review of the Two Teams' Artistry 169

North China Team

Goalkeeper: Huang Zhen-xun was calm and steady, saving the ball reliably and performing well. His slow response to the second goal seemed like a moment of carelessness.

Backs: Wang was better than Xian, but both often lost their footing, which was a flaw.

Center Back: Zhang Guo-wei was very good, providing strong support. The two on the left and right

Guards revealed gaps from time to time. Central China attacked from time to time. The two forwards did not defend rigorously.

Forwards: The five forwards coordinated well and were in good condition. The two wings were agile and fast, which was commendable and outstanding. The center forward dribbled the ball in all directions and was also very proper. Unfortunately, the biggest weakness was inaccurate shooting. So many great opportunities were missed.

Central China Team 170

Goalkeeper: The best player in the whole team, steady and reliable. It was not easy to maintain this under such severe pressure. The final goal was not his fault.

Backs: The weakest point of the Central China team. They lost their footing countless times, and the ball went in all directions.

Center Back: The center back Yu Ke-ding was very good, providing excellent support from time to time. Unfortunately, the two forwards were also too weak. They could not defend when retreating, nor could they attack when advancing.

Forwards: Yuan Qing-wu stood out. Wang Yi-de was slow. Although the two wings were brave, they were not fast. Their hearts were willing, but their bodies were not strong enough. Looking at the two teams as a whole, the common major problem was the slowness of action, especially Central China. They did not go to find the ball, but waited, which was impossible. Furthermore, the lack of direction in shooting was a major reason why they could not succeed greatly. Losing the ball was the most dangerous thing. Being able to control the fate of the entire army. The backs of the two teams showed this from time to time. These are things that athletes should strive to improve. Although, gathering temporarily, achieving such results is not easy.
